  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6557665e-db64-4514-a70b-b466f3d173cd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText3040334415635989011" style="display:none">"Emotional Intelligence 2.0 succinctly explains how to deal with emotions creatively and employ our intelligence in a beneficial way."<br />--THE DALAI LAMA<br /><br />For the first time ever in a book, TalentSmart's revolutionary program helps people identify their EQ skills, build these skills into strengths, and enjoy consistent performance in the pursuit of important life objectives. The book contains proven strategies from a decade-long effort to accurately measure and increase emotional intelligence. Trusted by upper-echelon leaders inside companies worldwide, these strategies will enable you to capitalize on the skills responsible for 58% of performance in all types of jobs.<br /><br />Includes a passcode for online access to the world's bestselling emotional intelligence test, the Emotional Intelligence Appraisal®, which will show you where your EQ stands today and what you can do to begin maximizing it immediately.<br /><br />Rooted in sound research involving more than 500,000 responses, this new edition of the test will:<br /><br />--Pinpoint which of the book's 66 emotional intelligence strategies will increase your EQ the most.<br /><br />--Reveal the specific behaviors responsible for your EQ scores.<br /><br />--Allow you to test yourself a second time to measure how much your EQ has increased from your efforts.<br /><br />The book's smooth narrative style turns rigorous research into memorable stories and practical strategies that anyone can use to his or her advantage.<br /><br /><b>With 90% of top performers high in EQ, and EQ twice as important as IQ in getting where you want to go in life, who can afford to ignore it?</b><br /><br />What people are saying about it:<br /><br />"Emotional Intelligence 2.0 is a fast read with compelling anecdotes and good context in which to understand and improve your score."<br />--Newsweek<br /><br />"Surveys of 500,000 people on the role of emotions in daily life have enabled the authors to hone EQ assessment to a 28-question online survey that can be completed in seven minutes."<br />--The Washington Post<br /><br />"Read worthy strategies for improving emotional intelligence skills make this our how-to book of the week. It's nice to know that average IQ doesn't limit a person to average performance. And who can resist an online quiz with instant feedback?"<br />--Newsday<br /><br />"Gives abundant, practical findings and insights with emphasis on how to develop EQ. Research shows convincingly that EQ is more important than IQ."<br />--Stephen R. Covey, author, The 7 Habits of Highly Effective People<br /><br />"This book can drastically change the way you think about success...read it twice."<br />--Patrick Lencioni, author, The Five Dysfunctions of a Team<br /><br />"At last a book that gives how to's rather than just what to's. We need no more convincing that emotional intelligence is at the core of life success. What we need are practical ways of improving it. Bradberry and Greaves brilliant new book is a godsend. It will change your life."<br />--Joseph Grenny, New York Times bestselling coauthor of Crucial Conversations<br /><br />"Emotional intelligence is an extremely important skill for personal and professional success. This book is excellent and the learning included in the free online test is cutting-edge. I strongly recommend it."<br />--Ken Blanchard, bestselling business book author of all time; coauthor The One Minute Manager®<br /><br />"I distributed the book to my entire team. We found it very helpful in our dealings with each other and our internal customers. With all the new buzzwords over the past few years, the heart and soul of a company's culture is how they support and promote emotional intelligence. Those with foresight see that emotional intelligence will separate the good companies from the great ones. This book is a wonderful tool for a grass roots approach. If your desire is to be a truly resonate leader that people will trust and follow, this is an opportunity that cannot only change your professional career, but also your personal relationships."<br />--Regina Sacha, vice president, human resources, FedEx Custom Critical<br /><br />"In the fast lane of business life today, people spend more time on computer keyboards, blackberries and conference calls than they do in face-to-face communication. We're expected to piece together broken conversations, cryptic voicemails, and abbreviated text messages to figure out how to proceed. In this increasingly complex web, emotional intelligence is more important than ever before. This book is filled with invaluable insights and information that no one can afford to ignore."<br />--Rajeev Peshawaria, executive director, Goldman Sachs International</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Not very. However, neither would any book be. It's not about reading the book it's about using what you have learned over and over and over again. It'<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Not very. However, neither would any book be. It's not about reading the book it's about using what you have learned over and over and over again. It's about thinking about what you are reading. Stopping taking notes, rereading, thinking than doing. If you do exactly what any book tells you to do, guaranteed that book would have astronomical impacts on your life. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_659167069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/659167069" />
    <a title="Tanya Tosheva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5988627-tanya-tosheva"><img alt="Tanya Tosheva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492637056p2/5988627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/659167069?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya Tosheva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya Tosheva" href="/user/show/5988627-tanya-tosheva">Tanya Tosheva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5988627-tanya-tosheva?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer659167069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14662343229479297219">This is a textbook example of how <i>not</i> to write a scientific book. Admittedly, the book never claims to be scientific but it supposedly concerns emotional intelligence - a psychological concept - and its effects on our daily lives. Yet there's not a single experiment mentioned.<br/><br/>My favorite parts were:<br/><br/>"Here’s how it works: everything you see, smell, hear, taste and touch travels through your body in the form of electric signals. These signals pass from cell to cell until they reach their ultimate d</span>
  <span id="freeText14662343229479297219" style="display:none">This is a textbook example of how <i>not</i> to write a scientific book. Admittedly, the book never claims to be scientific but it supposedly concerns emotional intelligence - a psychological concept - and its effects on our daily lives. Yet there's not a single experiment mentioned.<br /><br />My favorite parts were:<br /><br />"Here’s how it works: everything you see, smell, hear, taste and touch travels through your body in the form of electric signals. These signals pass from cell to cell until they reach their ultimate destination, your brain. They enter your brain at the base near the spinal cord, but must travel to your frontal lobe (behind your forehead) before reaching the place where rational, logical thinking takes place. The trouble is, they pass through your limbic system along the way—the place where emotions are produced. This journey ensures you experience things emotionally before your reason can kick into gear."<br /><br />"People with the highest levels of intelligence (IQ) outperform those with average IQs just 20 percent of the time, while people with average IQs outperform those with high IQs 70 percent of the time." <br /><br />Great... but are these results based on an actual experiment?<br /><br />"Only 36 percent of the people we tested are able to accurately identify their emotions as they happen. This means that two thirds of us are typically controlled by our emotions and are not yet skilled at spotting them and using them to our benefit." <br /><br />You sound very confident that your sample is representative. I, however, am <i>not</i>. How many people did you test? What kind of methods did you use?<br /><br />"There is no known connection between IQ and EQ; you simply can’t predict EQ based on how smart someone is. Cognitive intelligence, or IQ, is not flexible. Your IQ, short of a traumatic event such as a brain injury, is fixed from birth. You don’t get smarter by learning new facts or information. Intelligence is your ability to learn, and it’s the same at age 15 as it is at age 50. EQ, on the other hand, is a flexible skill that can be learned"<br /><br />Experiments proving these statements?<br /><br />"We’ve tested EQ alongside 33 other important workplace behaviors and found that it subsumes the majority of them, including time management, decision-making, and communication. Your EQ is the foundation for a host of critical skills—it impacts most everything you say and do each day. EQ is so critical to success that it accounts for 58 percent of performance in all types of jobs. It’s the single biggest predictor of performance in the workplace and the strongest driver of leadership and personal excellence."<br /><br />"Of all the people we’ve studied at work, we have found that 90 percent of high performers are also high in EQ. On the flip side, just 20 percent of low performers are high in EQ. You can be a high performer without EQ, but the chances are slim."<br /><br />"<b>Naturally, people with high EQs make more money—an average of $29,000 more per year than people with low EQs. The link between EQ and earnings is so direct that every point increase in EQ adds $1,300 to an annual salary. These findings hold true for people in all industries, at all levels, in every region of the world. We haven’t yet been able to find a job in which performance and pay aren’t tied closely to EQ.</b>"<br /><br />I'm reluctant to place this on the non-fiction shelf.<br /><br />Two stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14662343229479297219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_173503632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173503632" />
    <a title="June" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5433722-june"><img alt="June" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173503632?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="June" class="user" itemprop="url" name="June" href="/user/show/5433722-june">June</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173503632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2752966715166883207">This is the first applied emotional intelligence book that I am reading. It has its pros (clarity and simplicity of content) and some cons (excessive self-promotion). <br/><br/>Cons<br/>1. Open the book and you are hit with several pages of endorsements from well-known people. Hard to miss the Dalai Lama's one as it is the first. <br/><br/>Further on, particularly towards the end of the book, it's evident that the authors could have practised some self-restraint in mentioning their company- the name-dropping is excessiv</span>
  <span id="freeText2752966715166883207" style="display:none">This is the first applied emotional intelligence book that I am reading. It has its pros (clarity and simplicity of content) and some cons (excessive self-promotion). <br /><br />Cons<br />1. Open the book and you are hit with several pages of endorsements from well-known people. Hard to miss the Dalai Lama's one as it is the first. <br /><br />Further on, particularly towards the end of the book, it's evident that the authors could have practised some self-restraint in mentioning their company- the name-dropping is excessive. <br /><br />When reading these sort of books, I prefer to judge it on its merits so I found this style of marketing and self-promotion to be quite off-putting and unnecessary. <br /><br />2. I wish that the test and scores were freely available i.e. to friends and acquaintances who are sceptics or curious about EQ. Given that people have to purchase the book to access the strategies, a better approach might have been to offer the test for free, along with a sample strategy for each area. It also assumes that people have easy access to the internet- which they may not. <br /><br />3. Some readers may not click with the casual conversational tone of the book. There is a literal peppering of "it's", which make me cringe. <br /><br />Pros<br />1. I like that their explanations are not riddled with jargon (or as dense compared to the original Emotional Intelligence)- information is easily digestible and more likely to stick with me. <br /><br />I can see how the content might be criticised as over-simplistic but I'm treating it as food for thought that you can take in and practice at my own pace. <br /><br />Similarly, strategies are framed in such a way that I can attempt to try them out amidst a busy schedule. A quick skim of the strategies revealed quite a few that I hadn't come across before in previous reading on cognitive restructuring. <br /><br />2. I like the logical structure of the book and the case examples are a great inclusion. I identified with characteristics found in those who had high and low EQ. <br /><br />3. Physically, the book is a good sized hardback that's light enough to tote around. <br /><br />I haven't finished the book and will update this post when I have. Despite its flaws, I think it will be a useful introduction to developing improved EQ- I have family members who would really benefit from reading it. =P </span>
  <a data-text-id="2752966715166883207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150721506?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie" href="/user/show/816852-laurie">Laurie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150721506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9390780106376169314">I really wish I had read this book in high school and better yet had a course in it. It would have saved me a lot of grief. As a society, we need to teach children how to deal with emotions. I wish I had not taken it out of the library because the code in the back only works for one person. So, I was not able to take the EQ (Emotional Intelligence)test. I may need to buy the book.<br/><br/>I loved it all, but I have picked out my favorite parts of each section:<br/><br/>Self Awareness Strategies:<br/><br/>1. Ask others for f</span>
  <span id="freeText9390780106376169314" style="display:none">I really wish I had read this book in high school and better yet had a course in it. It would have saved me a lot of grief. As a society, we need to teach children how to deal with emotions. I wish I had not taken it out of the library because the code in the back only works for one person. So, I was not able to take the EQ (Emotional Intelligence)test. I may need to buy the book.<br /><br />I loved it all, but I have picked out my favorite parts of each section:<br /><br />Self Awareness Strategies:<br /><br />1. Ask others for feedback about how you handle your emotions and listen carefully to what they say.<br />2. Weekly or bi-weekly take stock of your life and write down situations that you didn't deal with well and then list which quality that you wanted to honor but didn't. For example:<br />Honesty is the quality and then write down a situation that I didn't handle well where I wasn't completely honest. The next time a situation like this comes up, I might deal with it differently because I will remember the list.<br /><br />Self Management Strategies:<br /><br />1. To prepare for change, make a list of things in my life that could possibly change and write down ideas for how I could deal with that. I really enjoyed doing this and it really has been helpful.<br /><br />Social Awareness Strategies:<br /><br />1. Become a great observer. Learn how to sense the mood of a room and check to see if your observations are correct.<br />1. Listen. Listen. Listen. Don't interrupt.<br /><br />Relationship Management Strategies:<br /><br />1. Use these phrases more: "I am sorry." "Please" "Thank You"<br /><br />Fabulous book. I highly recommend it.</span>

<div id="review_178067160" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178067160" />
    <a title="Keith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3074982-keith"><img alt="Keith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1261850552p2/3074982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178067160?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keith" href="/user/show/3074982-keith">Keith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3074982-keith?shelf=self-help">self-help</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178067160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2547730488533256227">I put off reading this book because there were other books that I marked to read before it. Once I started reading it, it was a quick interesting read, and I was glad that I moved it ahead of other books in the queue. <br/><br/>Some of the strategies in the four sections of the book felt like they were closely related. <br/><br/>I look forward to working on increasing my EQ by using the assessment test to determine where I need to focus my efforts and applying the relevant strategies from the 66 strategies listed i</span>
  <span id="freeText2547730488533256227" style="display:none">I put off reading this book because there were other books that I marked to read before it. Once I started reading it, it was a quick interesting read, and I was glad that I moved it ahead of other books in the queue. <br /><br />Some of the strategies in the four sections of the book felt like they were closely related. <br /><br />I look forward to working on increasing my EQ by using the assessment test to determine where I need to focus my efforts and applying the relevant strategies from the 66 strategies listed in the book.<br /><br />Emotional Intelligence 2.0 Strategies<br /><br /> <pre>
  <b>1. Self Awareness Strategies</b>
</pre><br />1. Quit treating your feelings as good or bad<br />2. Observe the ripple effect from your emotions<br />3. Lean into your discomfort<br />4. Feel your emotions physically<br />5. Know who and what pushes your buttons<br />6. Watch yourself like a hawk ...<br />7. Keep a journal about your emotions<br />8. Don't be fooled by a bad mood<br />9. Don't be fooled by a good mood either<br />10. Stop and ask yourself why you do the things you do.<br />11. Visit your values<br />12. Check yourself<br />13. Spot your emotions in books, movies, and music<br />14. Seek feedback<br />15 Get to know yourself under stress<br /><br /> <pre>
  <b>2. Self-Management Strategies</b>
</pre><br />1. Breath right<br />2. Create an emotion vs. reason list<br />3. Make your goals public<br />4. Count to ten<br />5. Sleep on it<br />6. Talk to a skilled self-manager<br />7. Smile and laugh more<br />8. Set aside some time in your day for problem solving<br />9. Take control of your self-talk<br />10. Visualize yourself succeeding<br />11. Clean up your sleep hygine<br />12. Focus your attention on your freedoms, rather than your limitations<br />13. Stay synchronized<br />14. Speak to someone who is not emotionally invesed in your problem<br />15. learn a valuable lesson from everyone you encounter<br />16. Put a mental recharge into your schedule<br />17. Accept that change is just around the corner (Risk Analysis)<br /><br /> <pre>
  <b>3. Social Awareness Strategies</b>
</pre><br />1. Greet people by name<br />2. Watch body language<br />3. Make timing everything<br />4. Develop a back-pocket question<br />5. Don't take notes at meetings<br />6. Plan ahead for social gatherings<br />7. Clear away the clutter<br />8. Live in the moment<br />9. Go on on a 15-minute tour<br />10. Watch EQ at the movies<br />11. Practice the art of listening<br />12. Go people watching<br />13. Understand the rules of the culture game<br />14. Test for accuracy<br />15. Step into their shoes<br />16. Seek the whole picture<br />17. Catch the mood of the room<br /><br /> <pre>
  <b>4. Relationship Management Strategies</b>
</pre><br />1. Be open and curious<br />2. Enhance your natural communication style<br />3. Avoid giving mixed signals<br />4. Remember the little things that pack a punch<br />5. Take feedback well<br />6. Build trust<br />7. Have an "Open-door" policy<br />8. Only get mad on purpose<br />9. Don't avoid the inevitable<br />10. Acknowledge the other person's feelings<br />11. Complement the person's emotions or situations<br />12. When you care, show it<br />13. Explain your decisions, don't just make them<br />14. Make your feedback direct and constructive<br />15. Allin your Intetion with your Impact<br />16. Offer a "Fix-it" statement during a broken conversation<br />17. Tackle a tough conversation<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2547730488533256227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1849469788715651455" style="display:none">After I took the emotional intelligence test and recieved my score, I was a little upset that I was merely average in my score. I would like to think I'm above average, but don't we all? One of my professors last semester opened class with the statement "Most if not everyone in this room thinks they are above average, I'm sorry but you are not."<br /><br />Low and behold there was hope, the coping strategies and techniques provided in this book to help you work on your area of weakness.<br /><br />While reading the examples given for each strength and the good and bad examples I was surprised to find that I resembled a few of the bad examples in previous work experience. Looking back I wish I could change how I handled my old job, and maybe it would have had a better outcome (rather than what did happen, where I resent almost everyone I worked with). <br /><br />Hope is not lost, now I can move forward and hopefully redirect my current ways of interacting with others. It will take me a few months to practice better habits but hopefully I can use these new suggestions to insure success during my summer internship!</span>

<div id="review_1096958630" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1096958630" />
    <a title="Molly Octopus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3184470-molly-octopus"><img alt="Molly Octopus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370208562p2/3184470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1096958630?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly Octopus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly Octopus" href="/user/show/3184470-molly-octopus">Molly Octopus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1096958630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6308110944618751981">Disclosure: I received this book for free via Goodreads book giveaways.<br/><br/><br/>Emotional intelligence. The concept has been floating around for so long that it would be easy for one to assume that it's a scientifically validated theory-- like IQ and personality measurements (which this book presents EQ alongside).<br/><br/>Unfortunately, as anyone who has done enough careful study knows, none of these three concepts are nearly as solid as many believe. EQ is the worst offender of all. Scientists have had incredib</span>
  <span id="freeText6308110944618751981" style="display:none">Disclosure: I received this book for free via Goodreads book giveaways.<br /><br /><br />Emotional intelligence. The concept has been floating around for so long that it would be easy for one to assume that it's a scientifically validated theory-- like IQ and personality measurements (which this book presents EQ alongside).<br /><br />Unfortunately, as anyone who has done enough careful study knows, none of these three concepts are nearly as solid as many believe. EQ is the worst offender of all. Scientists have had incredible difficulty even measuring it accurately, let alone confirming it actually exists as currently imagined-- to the point that it's scientifically irresponsible to write a book without explaining the scientific caveats, especially one declaring it the most important factor of personal success.<br /><br />And indeed, the entire book is a prime example of bad science. Here are some great examples of the book's various claims, NONE OF WHICH HAVE CITATIONS:<br /><br />"EQ is so critical to success that it accounts for 58 percent of performance in all types of jobs (pg. 20)"<br /><br />"The link between EQ and earnings is so direct that every point increase in EQ adds $1,300 to an annual salary (pg. 21)"<br /><br />And my personal favorite:<br /><br />"Only 36 percent of the people we tested are able to accurately identify their emotions as they happen (pg. 14)"<br /><br />Wow! That sounds amazingly scientific! How ever did you measure that?<br /><br />Looks like we'll never know.<br /><br />(Note: the "citations" are hidden in the back of the book under the "Notes" section. Perhaps the author didn't want any science cluttering his bullshit. Or maybe he wanted to create the illusion that he invented all the concepts the wrote about instead of stealing them and reproducing them into a terrible book to make easy money off suckers.)<br /><br /><br /><br />Further complaints:<br />1. The book opens with 7 pages of endorsements. Ugh.<br />2. The introduction contains small text boxes that quote (or rephrase) pieces from the same page, in the style of a magazine or newspaper article. I'm can't be the only person who finds this practice ridiculously annoying.<br />3. All of the self-improvement strategies are recycled garbage from every other self-help book on the market. Keep a journal. Think about your values. Count to ten.<br />4. The last 4 pages try to sell you more stuff.<br /><br /><br />Final Thoughts:<br />I used to be against book burning, but now I'm not so sure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6308110944618751981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_405915359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/405915359" />
    <a title="Loy Machedo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7118702-loy-machedo"><img alt="Loy Machedo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470479810p2/7118702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/405915359?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Loy Machedo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Loy Machedo" href="/user/show/7118702-loy-machedo">Loy Machedo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer405915359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15083189450365804644"><br/>Loy Machedo’s Book Review – Emotional Intelligence 2.0 by Travis Bradberry & Jean Greaves<br/><br/>Just think about this.<br/><br/>You have a recommendation from The Dalai Lama, Newsweek, The Washington Post, Newsday, Ken Blanchard and Marshall Goldsmith. And then to top it all, you have a foreword by (Ouch!) Patrick Lencioni himself!<br/><br/>Now do you need any other reason to be convinced why you should buy this book?<br/><br/>Wait! Don’t.<br/><br/>Before you decide to purchase this book, read the rest and only then decide.<br/><br/>Review in a nutshe</span>
  <span id="freeText15083189450365804644" style="display:none"><br />Loy Machedo’s Book Review – Emotional Intelligence 2.0 by Travis Bradberry &amp; Jean Greaves<br /><br />Just think about this.<br /><br />You have a recommendation from The Dalai Lama, Newsweek, The Washington Post, Newsday, Ken Blanchard and Marshall Goldsmith. And then to top it all, you have a foreword by (Ouch!) Patrick Lencioni himself!<br /><br />Now do you need any other reason to be convinced why you should buy this book?<br /><br />Wait! Don’t.<br /><br />Before you decide to purchase this book, read the rest and only then decide.<br /><br />Review in a nutshell.<br />1. The Chapter opens up with the gripping story of a Surfer who fought and survived against a Great White Shark.<br />2. We learn what EQ is all about and what it isn’t, along with research material, illustrations and anecdotes.<br />3. The 4 skills of Emotional Intelligence - Self-Awareness, Self-Management, Social Awareness, and Relationship Management.<br />4. 6 Steps Action Plan to Increase Emotional Intelligence Levels.<br />5. 15 Self-Awareness Strategies<br />6. 17 Self-Management Strategies<br />7. 17 Social-Awareness Strategies<br />8. 17 Relationship Management Strategies<br />9. Latest Research &amp; Discoveries in the world of Emotional Intelligence.<br /><br />That is exactly what the whole book is about.<br /><br />A few drawbacks of this book are:<br />1) Most of the strategies are outright simple, silly or at times childish.<br />2) The book tempts you to take a website based test – which is again very basic but at the same time exposes you to a heavily marketed number of tests (good sales strategy I will admit)<br />3) Personally, I doubt you will follow all these techniques for more than a few weeks. Eventually, it will be like joining a gym for a year, going for hardcore exercises for the first few weeks and then never again getting off the couch-based-TV-phase for the rest of your life.<br /><br />Now, I do not want to get into explaining in detail the tricks, tips and strategies of the book simply because it be right. But I will give credit to the authors for being honest - the final chapter says it best – if these strategies are not practiced regularly, it is like a muscle that is not trained – You will lose your flexibility and strength.<br /><br />So now should you buy or not buy this book?<br /><br />Here is the deal.<br /><br />This is a simple down to earth book with common sense being explained to the level of a child with a simple straight forward confession that no virtue will last it is regularly practiced. Period. It is nothing extra-ordinary, earth-shattering or mind blowing. However, just like exercising and eating healthy - it is doable and useful. But now the question is – How long? Why? When? And for What Reason?<br /><br />Quite Frankly, (and yes, In my humble opinion) I have come to realize, some people are born idiots and will remain idiots – irrespective which ever book they read. For instance, in my case, I am in-your-face with a don’t-care-a-dam attitude and a choice of behaviors that would get me terminated from any corporate constipated organization in a jiffy. I mean why should be anything else when I am enjoying a level of success and able to stay away from a few many bozo’s who are either dumb, ignorant or outright stupid? Irrespective which ever book I read, I believe there are some human being who should be exterminated from the face of the earth or kept in the zoos for the mentally retarded – given the fact they are back-stabbers, characterless and two faced. (In case you are bothered by this statement, it simply means this is your personality). So now, does reading this book make me a Male Version of Mother Teresa?<br /><br />Absolutely not.<br /><br />So here is my final verdict.I would recommend you to purchase this book only if you are willing to commit yourself to practicing these techniques of self-control, discipline and mental silence every single day with enough stamina to last a life time.<br />Otherwise, do yourself a favor, use common sense, patience, meditation with a bit of fasting and avoid purchasing this book altogether. It would do you a whole lot of favors and yes, save your money from purchasing another good book and making it catch dust among the few books you have at home.<br /><br />Overall Rating – 10 out of 10.<br /><br />Loy Machedo<br />loymachedo.com</span>
  <a data-text-id="15083189450365804644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_879708039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_687686576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/687686576" />
    <a title="Longfellow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/964474-longfellow"><img alt="Longfellow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204695199p2/964474.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/687686576?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Longfellow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Longfellow" href="/user/show/964474-longfellow">Longfellow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer687686576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7467478465444458892"><br/>If you want it to be, this book can be a quick 250 pages of helpful tips. It will probably be more useful, though, read over a few days or even a few weeks, allowing time to practice some of these recommendations or reflect on them with thought or in writing.<br/><br/>A few years ago, a counselor recommended the book <i>Ten Days to Self-Esteem</i>. I worked through its content enough to conclude its operating theory was that how one thinks controls how one feels. While I discovered this approach could yield some</span>
  <span id="freeText7467478465444458892" style="display:none"><br />If you want it to be, this book can be a quick 250 pages of helpful tips. It will probably be more useful, though, read over a few days or even a few weeks, allowing time to practice some of these recommendations or reflect on them with thought or in writing.<br /><br />A few years ago, a counselor recommended the book <i>Ten Days to Self-Esteem</i>. I worked through its content enough to conclude its operating theory was that how one thinks controls how one feels. While I discovered this approach could yield some positive results, I was disappointed that it did little to reveal what things might be at the root of why I had the feelings I did.<br /><br /><i>Emotional Intelligence 2.0</i> operates on a similar philosophy but with some nuances that make it a more satisfying self-help book, at least for me. One of these is that it begins with a physiological explanation of how emotions are produced. When our body sends signals to the brain, the transmission passes through the part of our brain that registers emotions <i>before</i> it reaches the part of our brain that produces rational thought. So emotions are in essence our first response to any situation and appear naturally before we deduce why we are feeling them. This is useful knowledge.<br /><br />Considering this reality, emotional self-awareness becomes the foundation of emotional intelligence. There are, of course, additional necessary steps to improve EI, but without this awareness, we cannot proceed on to the steps which will actually lead to healthier and more productive behaviors.<br /><br /><i>EI 2.0</i> contains various tips to increase self-awareness, but a couple of them serve as particularly good reminders for me. First, we are cautioned to stop labeling our emotions as either good or bad. Within the physiological context provided, this makes a lot of sense; initially, all emotions are responses, not things that we have evaluated and made a moral judgment on. Second, when we refuse to label our emotions as either good or bad, we are able to receive them rather than fight them, and in receiving them we can then evaluate why we are feeling the way we are. When we arrive at this evaluative process, we’re then able to identify “triggers” and other causes for various emotions. Once we understand these root causes, we are able to make decisions that can lead us to having more control over situations and reactions. It all makes great sense. And all this info is in just the first of four sections.<br /><br />While much of this information is not new, like many things that lead to better decision making and healthier behavior, it is good—essential even—to be reminded now and then and to see old or forgotten ideas from a fresh perspective.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7467478465444458892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer773189862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10303686801548646703">DISCLAIMER: I received this book as part of a free GoodReads giveaway.<br/><br/>This little gem is a short read. I finished it in approximately seven hours, and that included taking exhaustive notes. This book doesn’t take 10,000 pages to say 250 pages worth, and I appreciate that. It packs short, concise definitions and concrete, actionable takeaways. Truly a breath of fresh air.<br/><br/>I’ve read too many books at the end of which I have no clue how to apply the things I’ve learned. This book is not one of them.</span>
  <span id="freeText10303686801548646703" style="display:none">DISCLAIMER: I received this book as part of a free GoodReads giveaway.<br /><br />This little gem is a short read. I finished it in approximately seven hours, and that included taking exhaustive notes. This book doesn’t take 10,000 pages to say 250 pages worth, and I appreciate that. It packs short, concise definitions and concrete, actionable takeaways. Truly a breath of fresh air.<br /><br />I’ve read too many books at the end of which I have no clue how to apply the things I’ve learned. This book is not one of them. Every single strategy is immediately actionable and well illustrated with real-world examples.<br /><br />Another thing I really appreciate about this book is its organization. All its strategies are neatly organized into the four major categories of EQ skills for easy look-up and reviewal. I intend to keep this book close at hand for those days I need a quick refresher.<br /><br />Some have mentioned that this book seemed too self-promoting for their taste. I have to admit, there was a bit of this, but it all seemed to be pretty well contained in the introduction and conclusion, so you could skip over it if such things bother you, though I didn’t personally find it distasteful.<br /><br />All-in-all, a very enjoyable, short, and practical read. Highly recommended to anyone interested in emotional intelligence and how they can start improving theirs right away.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12680031177032076691">Fantastic book! I think this should be required reading for everyone at some point in their lives. Emotional Intelligence (EQ) is something we should all be aware of and it consists of Self-Awareness, Self-Management, Social Awareness, and Relationship Management. This book gives specific strategies to increase our awareness in these areas. If we are conscious of how our emotions affect us and the people around us, we can use that to make better choices. I won this book in a Goodreads giveaway a</span>
  <span id="freeText12680031177032076691" style="display:none">Fantastic book! I think this should be required reading for everyone at some point in their lives. Emotional Intelligence (EQ) is something we should all be aware of and it consists of Self-Awareness, Self-Management, Social Awareness, and Relationship Management. This book gives specific strategies to increase our awareness in these areas. If we are conscious of how our emotions affect us and the people around us, we can use that to make better choices. I won this book in a Goodreads giveaway and I am so happy that I did. I really wanted this book because I have a son who is highly intelligent, but I also want him to learn about EQ. This book comes with a passcode to the Emotional Intelligence Appraisal test and I am going to let my son use it. This book is a valuable resource for anyone and I highly recommend it!</span>

<div id="review_1053367899" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1053367899" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33637824-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476425665p2/33637824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1053367899?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/33637824-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1053367899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer241633346273471629">Emotional Intelligence 2.0 is a thoroughly researched and extensively explained discovery, unveiling and application of the vital skills of human self-awareness and discernment. The supporting theories, findings, suggestions and techniques are sound and invaluable for the human experience. This book is a critical step in the right direction for people everywhere in the world.<br/><br/>One significant criticism I have is the book's focus on negative aspects of relationships, personal emotions and generally</span>
  <span id="freeText241633346273471629" style="display:none">Emotional Intelligence 2.0 is a thoroughly researched and extensively explained discovery, unveiling and application of the vital skills of human self-awareness and discernment. The supporting theories, findings, suggestions and techniques are sound and invaluable for the human experience. This book is a critical step in the right direction for people everywhere in the world.<br /><br />One significant criticism I have is the book's focus on negative aspects of relationships, personal emotions and generally negative aspects of each individual's experience. Traditional psychology practices much the same techniques, so it's not completely surprising to find this focus. I was disappointed at the opportunity missed to introduce the well researched and factually supported techniques developed over the last forty years for immediate management of human emotions, including; Thought Field Therapy, Bio Energetic Synchronization Technique and I-Ching. Had these and many other available techniques been included, I would have been proud to rate Emotional Intelligence 2.0 with five stars.<br /><br />However, my criticism is not meant to cause a potential reader to pause. This information can be the perfect introduction to a whole new world of self-awareness, self-empowerment, discernment and possibly true success and happiness in life.<br /><br />A very important part of the puzzle of life has been shared in Emotional Intelligence 2.0. Now go get the rest and enjoy the journey!</span>
  <a data-text-id="241633346273471629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3831174825762435769">This was such a quick but also very informative read on emotional intelligence. It used examples to clearly illustrate why EQ is important to each one of us. The first section outlines what it is, and how it's different than IQ and personality, then it explains each aspect (there are 4) that make up the EQ. Then the book gives practical ideas to help the reader intentionally address each of the 4 parts of the EQ, to be more aware and to improve. I didn't read too closely these sections since I h</span>
  <span id="freeText3831174825762435769" style="display:none">This was such a quick but also very informative read on emotional intelligence. It used examples to clearly illustrate why EQ is important to each one of us. The first section outlines what it is, and how it's different than IQ and personality, then it explains each aspect (there are 4) that make up the EQ. Then the book gives practical ideas to help the reader intentionally address each of the 4 parts of the EQ, to be more aware and to improve. I didn't read too closely these sections since I had not taken an EQ test yet, but I had a general idea of where I could improve and found the ideas to be helpful. This is definitely something I want to look into more sometime!</span>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_26329'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26329.Emotional_Intelligence"><img alt="Emotional Intelligence: Why It Can Matter More Than IQ" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1388185411l/26329._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m9qb6jj06P/P4pvUUzio4F81sHLtvBX0bEa+ppTD+3VUQzeK4Ux4RzWtVwfrR2ejL8EMC/PdppfsrsJARNUV7g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wUW4i/apjH+2hiXlLToRl+9VSrM8ep35Q9b/c4Ot8/gO3BTrLxEcx0zJ6TaVRd7Un6H2yiIbLprDPoOVU7sdYw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

This is definitely true because we still see so much failure all around us. Now, I am not saying that by using Covey’s model, or anyone else’s model for that matter, you can become a sure-shot success, but at least we should have seen many more successes around us already judging by the number of copies the book has sold! So, where is the shortcoming?There are two main problems here, and we are talking only about the people who have read the book already. The first problem is that most people are too lazy to implement the ideals of Stephen Covey in their lives. They consider his masterpiece of a book as a mere coffee-table book or a book that you use for light reading when you are traveling and then forget all about it. They do not realize that this book contains life-changing information. Or, they take the information and do not make the effort to actually utilize it so that it becomes knowledge for them.The second problem is that a lot of people have a myopic view of Covey’s ideals. These are people who are impressed by the book already. If you ask them what the seven habits are, they can rattle them off end to end, but then they miss the larger picture. They do not understand that Covey was trying to tell more than he wrote in words. There are hidden implications in this book, yes, and a lot of people have just failed to see through them.That is what we are trying to do. We are trying to show you how Covey’s book, or rather, his model, was a complete model in itself. There was nothing amiss about it. If you implement it, there should be no aspect of your life that should go untouched. The only thing is that you have to understand these ideals and try to implement them in your life.But, before we barge into that area, it is extremely important to understand what these ideals are. What was the model that was propounded by Stephen Covey in his mega-famous book? The findings will surprise many readers and, quite frankly, upset others.\n\nThe Challenge\nBuilt to Last, the defining management study of the nineties, showed how great companies triumph over time and how long-term sustained performance can be engineered into the DNA of an enterprise from the very beginning. \n\nBut what about the company that is not born with great DNA? How can good companies, mediocre companies, even bad companies achieve enduring greatness? \n\nThe Study\nFor years, this question preyed on the mind of Jim Collins. Are there companies that defy gravity and convert long-term mediocrity or worse into long-term superiority? And if so, what are the universal distinguishing characteristics that cause a company to go from good to great?\n\nThe Standards\nUsing tough benchmarks, Collins and his research team identified a set of elite companies that made the leap to great results and sustained those results for at least fifteen years. How great? After the leap, the good-to-great companies generated cumulative stock returns that beat the general stock market by an average of seven times in fifteen years, better than twice the results delivered by a composite index of the world\'s greatest companies, including Coca-Cola, Intel, General Electric, and Merck. \n\nThe Comparisons\nThe research team contrasted the good-to-great companies with a carefully selected set of comparison companies that failed to make the leap from good to great. What was different? Why did one set of companies become truly great performers while the other set remained only good? \n\nThe Findings\nThe findings of the Good to Great study will surprise many readers and shed light on virtually every area of management strategy and practice. The findings include:\nLevel 5 Leaders: The research team was shocked to discover the type of leadership required to achieve greatness.\n\nThe Hedgehog Concept (Simplicity within the Three Circles): To go from good to great requires transcending the curse of competence.\n\nA Culture of Discipline: When you combine a culture of discipline with an ethic of entrepreneurship, you get the magical alchemy of great results. Technology Accelerators: Good-to-great companies think differently about the role of technology.\n\nThe Flywheel and the Doom Loop: Those who launch radical change programs and wrenching When buying a house, for example, it’s best to let our unconscious mull over the many variables. But when we’re picking a stock, intuition often leads us astray. <span id="freeTextContainer4790590056291696750">Dr. Travis Bradberry is the award-winning author of the #1 best selling book, Emotional Intelligence 2.0, and the cofounder of TalentSmart®⎯a consultancy that serves more than 75% of Fortune 500 companies and is the world’s leading provider of emotional intelligence tests and training.<br/><br/>His bestselling books have been translated into 25 languages and are available in more than 150 countries. Dr. Bra</span>
  <span id="freeText4790590056291696750" style="display:none">Dr. Travis Bradberry is the award-winning author of the #1 best selling book, Emotional Intelligence 2.0, and the cofounder of TalentSmart®⎯a consultancy that serves more than 75% of Fortune 500 companies and is the world’s leading provider of emotional intelligence tests and training.<br /><br />His bestselling books have been translated into 25 languages and are available in more than 150 countries. Dr. Bradberry has written for, or been covered by, Newsweek, BusinessWeek, Fortune, Forbes, Fast Company, Inc., USA Today, The Wall Street Journal, The Washington Post, and The Harvard Business Review.<br /><br />Dr. Bradberry is a world-renowned expert in emotional intelligence who speaks regularly in corporate and public settings. Example engagements include Intel, Coca-Cola, Microsoft, Fortune Brands, Boston Scientific, the Fortune Growth Summit, The Conference Board: Learning from Legends, the American Society for Training and Development, the Society for Human Resource Management, and Excellence in Government.<br /></span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
